## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The target variable dA_dt represents the instantaneous reaction rate in chemical kinetics, which typically depends on the concentration A according to the rate law of the reaction mechanism. The feature t may capture explicit time dependence, e.g., from catalyst deactivation or changing conditions, making this an autonomous or non-autonomous ordinary differential equation discovery task.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 (constant consumption rate independent of A)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A (exponential decay, rate proportional to A)
- Second-order dimerization: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of A)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general empirical reaction order)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (linear relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (quadratic, zero at A=0 and A=c1, maximum at intermediate A)
- Half-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * sqrt(A) (fractional order in heterogeneous catalysis or chain reactions)
- Substrate-inhibited rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A + A**2) (rate passes through a maximum then decreases with A)
- Hill-type cooperative rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (sigmoidal dependence on A)
- Time-decaying rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or temperature drop)
- Polynomial rate with time cross-term: dA_dt = c0 * A * t (rate increases linearly with time and concentration)
- Sum of production and consumption: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 - c2 (combines autocatalytic growth and higher-order decay)
- Reversible n-th order: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A)**c2 (generalized relaxation with power law)
- Combined order and decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 * exp(-c2 * t) (power-law in A and exponential decay in time)
- Exponential rate dependence: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * A) (rate grows exponentially with A, e.g., in autocatalytic runaway)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA/dt shows saturation as A increases (rate plateau), use Michaelis-Menten rational form A/(c + A) or Hill-type A^n/(c + A^n).
- If dA/dt crosses zero at a non-zero A, the reaction is reversible or involves an equilibrium; include a constant or linear offset like c0*(c1 - A).
- If dA/dt exhibits a maximum at intermediate A (bell shape), consider quadratic logistic form A*(c - A) or substrate inhibition A/(c0 + c1*A + A^2).
- If dA/dt vs A data on a log-log plot is linear, the reaction order is a constant power; use A^c for fractional order.
- If reaction rate decreases over time even at constant A, include an explicit time-dependent factor such as exp(-c*t).
- If the reaction network involves multiple elementary steps, dA/dt may be a sum of several monomials in A with different orders.
- Integer exponents (1,2,...) in rate law suggest elementary mass-action kinetics, while non-integer powers suggest complex or chain mechanisms.
- If dA/dt approaches zero as A goes to zero and also as A becomes very large, the rate law likely contains a denominator with A terms (saturation or inhibition).
- When A is consumed, dA/dt is negative; if A is a product, dA/dt positive; inclusion of both positive and negative terms models simultaneous production and consumption.
- An initial fast decay followed by a slow tail in A(t) often indicates a sum of first-order terms or a distribution of rate constants, which can sometimes be mimicked by a stretched exponential or power-law time dependence.
